I need to determine if any candidate formula can match the GT:

**GT:** `7.723*epsilon**3 + 36.659*epsilon**0.2144*exp(-82.437/(8.314*T)) + 1.336*epsilon*(T - 327.264)**2`

Let me expand the third term:
`1.336*epsilon*(T - 327.264)**2 = 1.336*epsilon*(T² - 654.529*T + 107,102.0)`
`= 1.336*epsilon*T² - 874.25*epsilon*T + 143,088.3*epsilon`

So GT = `7.723*epsilon**3 + 36.659*epsilon**0.2144*exp(-9.915/T) + 1.336*epsilon*T² - 874.25*epsilon*T + 143,088.3*epsilon`

The GT has these structural components:
1. `epsilon**3` term
2. `epsilon**0.2144 * exp(-c/T)` term (note: exp(-c/T), NOT exp(c*T))
3. `epsilon*T²` term
4. `epsilon*T` term
5. `epsilon` term

**Critical observation:** The exp term in the GT is `exp(-82.437/(8.314*T)) = exp(-9.915/T)`, which is `exp(-c/T)`. Most candidates use `exp(T*c)` or `exp(c*T)`, which is fundamentally different - `exp(c*T)` cannot equal `exp(-c/T)` for all T.

Let me check candidates with the right structure:

**Candidate 8:** `c0*epsilon**c1 + c2*epsilon**c3 + c4*epsilon**c5 + c6*epsilon*(T + c7)**c8`

Expanding `c6*epsilon*(T + c7)**c8` with c8=2: `c6*epsilon*(T + c7)² = c6*epsilon*T² + 2*c6*c7*epsilon*T + c6*c7²*epsilon`

This gives: `c0*epsilon**c1 + c2*epsilon**c3 + c4*epsilon**c5 + c6*epsilon*T² + 2*c6*c7*epsilon*T + c6*c7²*epsilon`

But the GT needs an `exp(-c/T)` term. The terms `c0*epsilon**c1 + c2*epsilon**c3 + c4*epsilon**c5` are all power-law terms in epsilon only (no T dependence), so they cannot produce `epsilon**0.2144 * exp(-9.915/T)`. **No match.**

**Candidate 70:** `T²*c0*epsilon + T*c1*epsilon + c2*epsilon**c3 + c4*epsilon + c5*epsilon*(T + c6)**c7`

With c7=2: `c5*epsilon*(T+c6)²` gives T², T, and constant terms in epsilon. Combined with the other T²*epsilon and T*epsilon terms, this gives `epsilon*(aT² + bT + d) + c2*epsilon**c3`. This has only one power-law term `epsilon**c3` without T-dependence. The GT needs both `epsilon**3` AND `epsilon**0.2144*exp(-9.915/T)`. The exp term can't be captured. **No match.**

**Candidate 72:** `T*c0*epsilon + c1*epsilon**c2 + c3*epsilon + c4*epsilon*(T + c5)**c6`

With c6=2: gives `epsilon*(c4*T² + (c0+2*c4*c5)*T + (c3+c4*c5²)) + c1*epsilon**c2`. Only one free power term. Can't match both epsilon**3 and the exp term. **No match.**

None of the candidates contain `exp(-c/T)` or `exp(c/T)` - they all use `exp(c*T)` or have no exponential at all. The GT fundamentally requires an `exp(-c/T)` term which none can replicate.

For candidates without exp: they'd need to match `epsilon**0.2144*exp(-9.915/T)` using non-exponential terms, which is impossible since this term depends on both epsilon and T in a specific exponential way.

After careful analysis, no candidate can match the GT because none can produce the `exp(-constant/T)` dependence present in the GT.

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `7.723*epsilon**3 + 36.659*epsilon**0.2144*exp(-82.437/(8.314*T)) + epsilon*1.336*(T - 327.264)**2`

Let me expand the last term:
`epsilon*1.336*(T - 327.264)**2 = epsilon*1.336*(T² - 654.529*T + 107,102.0) = 1.336*epsilon*T² - 874.449*epsilon*T + 143,088.3*epsilon`

So GT = `7.723*epsilon**3 + 36.659*epsilon**0.2144*exp(-9.916/T) + 1.336*epsilon*T² - 874.449*epsilon*T + 143,088.3*epsilon`

The GT has these basis functions:
1. `epsilon**3`
2. `epsilon**0.2144 * exp(-c/T)` (Arrhenius-type term)
3. `epsilon * T²`
4. `epsilon * T`
5. `epsilon`

The exp(-c/T) term is crucial - it's NOT the same as exp(c*T). Let me check candidates systematically.

**Key observations:**
- `exp(-c4/(c5*T))` = `exp(-9.916/T)` is NOT equivalent to `exp(c*T)` for any constant c
- The T-dependence through `(T-c)**2 * epsilon` expands to `T²*epsilon + T*epsilon + epsilon` terms
- Many candidates use `exp(T*c)` which cannot match `exp(-c/T)`

Let me check candidates that might have the right structure:

**Candidate 47:** `T**2*c0*epsilon + T*c1*epsilon + c2*epsilon**c3 + c4*epsilon + c5*epsilon**c6 + c7*epsilon**3`
= T²*epsilon term + T*epsilon term + epsilon**c3 + epsilon + epsilon**c6 + epsilon**3
This has no exp(-c/T) term. The GT's exp term can't be matched. But wait - can `epsilon**c6` absorb the exp term? No, because the exp term depends on T. **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 70:** `T**2*c0*epsilon + T*c1*epsilon + c2*epsilon**c3 + c4*epsilon + c5*epsilon*(T + c6)**c7`
The last term `c5*epsilon*(T+c6)**c7` - if c7=2, this gives `c5*epsilon*(T+c6)²` = `c5*epsilon*T² + 2*c5*c6*epsilon*T + c5*c6²*epsilon`. Combined with the first terms, we get `(c0+c5)*epsilon*T² + (c1+2*c5*c6)*epsilon*T + (c4+c5*c6²)*epsilon + c2*epsilon**c3`. But we still need the `exp(-c/T)` term AND `epsilon**3`. We can set c3=3 to get epsilon**3, but then we lose the exp term. The exp(-c/T) term cannot be represented. **[NO MATCH]**

Let me check if ANY candidate has `exp(-c/T)` or `exp(c/T)` structure... None do. Most have `exp(T*c)` or no exp at all.

**Candidate 8:** `c0*epsilon**c1 + c2*epsilon**c3 + c4*epsilon**c5 + c6*epsilon*(T + c7)**c8`
With c8=2: `c6*epsilon*(T+c7)²` gives the T²,T,constant epsilon terms. Set c1=3 for epsilon³. But we need `epsilon**0.2144*exp(-c/T)` which can't come from `epsilon**c3 + epsilon**c5`. **[NO MATCH]**

After careful analysis, NONE of the candidates contain an `exp(-c/T)` or equivalent Arrhenius term. The GT fundamentally requires this term, and it cannot be replicated by `exp(c*T)`, polynomials, logs, or sin functions.
